Amazing fusion of simple concepts, sushi and mexican flavors. Their Hot Cheetos Roll was really good and had just enough of that red spice for flavor to complement. The super micheladas are almost a meal themselves, large glasses filled with shrimp and other veggies marinating in a well made michelada with beer of your choice. < Name>
Brook Porter< /Name>
<date>1550584362381</date><rating>5< /rating>< Review>
Morris Graves is located in the restored Carnegie library building in Eureka, California and is a majestic building. The second-floor balcony is a rotunda, the walls of which hold works of current and local painters. It is named for a local artist who died on May 5, 2001 at his 380 acre lake home in Loleta,CA, a few miles South of Eureka. The building contains a small collection of Graves' many works and much of a personal collection of his collegues' paintings. Eureka is the hub of multiple beautiful surrounding locations and the show place of many artists. The works are changed regularly and the basement gift shop has many treats. Come on the first Saturday of every month for special shows of music, photography, painting, and sculpture that run from Morris Graves throughout the town.< /Review>

This beautiful old library building just off Old Town Eureka is a perfect art destination,  and the highlight of a recent art walk on First Saturday's Arts Alive.  The different size rooms allow for larger or small intimate displays.  A large area is perfect for performances and a band was adding to the festive atmosphere.  And the building's woodwork, columns, tile flooring have all been beautifully maintained to appreciate now and in the future.<//text>

< text>
Hands down the best Hawaiian food in Los Angeles.       I have tried a few things on the menu and everything has been absolutely delicious.    This is one of those places that is like if you don't know about it you would just drive by.    It's in a bowling alley and for me when I think bowling alley food I think roller hot dogs and greasy burgers.     But this place is the polar opposite good delicious food with a huge menu selection.    If you are in Gardena definitely check this place out.      Damn good food</text>

<Text>USA üá∫üá∏ (Hawai'i)
Eat the World LA review:
Besides Gardena and surrounding areas being home to many Hawaiians in Los Angeles, the image of a yellow hibiscus is the only clue that the food inside the coffee shop will include some Hawaiian specials. This species is the state's official flower and used often around the islands as a source of pride.

Even if this cute diner inside of Gardena Bowl did not offer a loco moco or King's Hawaiian bread, it would still be a fun place to come for breakfast. In fact, most customers were sticking with greasy spoon favorites paired with their coffee. The interior of the diner is what you think it might look like based on the 70's imagery from the bowling alley's sign above, a place that probably maxes out at 30 people when at capacity with booths lining two sides of the room.< /Text><Pictures>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMSMHQuQ07ewDGMNGv9_YhPAc5uFovmwiEo_k3-=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNwlKB7mxFMqzFRSM2ikShafNpHBuQNpD3JfLHo=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMub8ZxfIP8Hvl8O6VE4g3k0rGc2lMCug0PGuyP=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMMnuZtgg6-VtS28JvSxzyQWMT6weAlvk3aVNt0=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /Pictures>< resp>

< user_name>
Stephan Anglin<//user_name>
< date>
1582668792723< /date>
<Rate>5< /Rate>< review>
It was me and my wife's first time here, upon seeing it on Netflix's "Breakfast, Lunch and Dinner." We tried and loved their miso soup, the standard beef patty Loco Moco (the patties are made in-house), a side of Garlic Chicken, Hawaiian Royal, and a Portuguese Sausage patty on the side.
The miso soup was tasty, consisting of plenty of chopped scallions, noodles, and perfect dashi stock.
The 2 patties on the Loco Moco were huge and perfectly char-broiled.  They actually have 4 types of protein for their Loco Moco to chose from: beef patty, Portuguese sausage patty, Kalua, and Katsu chicken patty.  The side of the Portuguese patty was delicious with a slight kick of spice, but trumped in size compared to its beef alternative.
The Hawaiian Royal is a generously served dish of steamed rice beneath chunks of Portuguese sausage, Chashu (the reddish BBQ pork), chopped green onions & eggs drizzled with Teriyaki Sauce.  The dish was my favorite of the four, which worked out in my favor given the abundance of each ingredient in it.  It can easily be shared amongst two to three people.</review>

< text>
Awesome coffee shop! Definitely a local gem! Been coming here for the past 6 years and still to this day they stay true to it's menu. We ordered bacon fried rice, saimin, and corn beef hash. The prices are very reasonable and good. You would have to come early as this place gets crowded at times so don't wait too long. Awesome service! If you are a coffee drinker, this is the place for you. They make sure you cup is never empty. It's no Starbucks but it gets the job done.< /text>

< Text>
I love the food here.  It is delicious.  Everything from the breakfast items (served all day), especially the Portuguese Sausage (which is their own recipe and it's a patty type sausage not like a hot dog) and eggs and the Hawaiian Royale (a rice dish with eggs, portugese sausage, char siu, sauce, kind of like a fried rice but not).  The Japanese food is delicious, they do a great tempura.  Or if you just want a burger and fries you can't go wrong either.  So all the things needed to be a great little diner.< /Text>

At the beginning of April I did not receive any call or mail to let me know the status. I asked if the orange would arrive on 5/17 as expected and they told me it looked on time. I am coming from LA so I would want to go there only once. Around the 8th of May I get a call with an update. The orange one was now showing to be shipped a little later on 5/23 so they told me that it would be ready around the 30th for pick up. < review>
In the Summer of 2014 I purchased a Trek 8.4 DS bicycle. In the summer of 2019, just five years later, the plastic knob that locks/unlocks the suspension broke and no longer functioned. I was simply looking to replace this part for my less than five year old bike at the time that I have had garaged since I bought it. I took it to the Nearest Trek store and after having my bicycle for several days offered no resolution. I then contacted the corporate customer service department and spoke to Luke Borland who initially seemed like he wanted to help, but informed me that they do not stock replacement parts like the one I was looking for. The resolution offered to me was a new fork at a "discounted price" plus cost of labor. My bike and fork are blue, the colors they offered me were white and black. The fork they offered me would've cost approximately $150.00 and it wouldn't even match my fork. All i want is a lockout knob for my fork, and think it is unreasonable and unfair that a bike that I paid over $800.00 has completely degraded it's functionality. Even the Trek store in Bonita, CA that I brought it to initially told me that the bike I purchased is a "lower end bike" and I couldn't agree more at this point.¬† I think it is completely irresponsible of Trek to sell bikes and not offer replacement parts just five years later.< /review>

<review>BE CAREFUL buying here. Do your research on this place. As another reviewer said, "nice people, terrible service." This about sums it up. The people are all very nice and make you feel welcome. The actual service (so far) has been awful.

Why? They sold me a bike with a poorly chosen/installed component that broke and damaged the fork, then chose to take zero responsibility for it and essentially told me it wasn't their fault (I had owned it for a week and rode it only 7 miles, 6.9 of which were after the damage occurred). They then told me that don't accept returns (even if the reason for the return was their fault, like in my case) and told me my options were to exchange it for a more expensive bike (how convenient) or go buy nail polish and paint it myself. And I had paid them for the Velocare bike insurance, too. I mean, are you kidding me? Take responsibility for your store and your inventory, Trek. I made the mistake of trusting them, and it might've landed me in a potentially very costly long-term situation. I hope I'm an outlier and that they are otherwise accommodating, but who knows. Fingers crossed for better customer service in the future.

All that said, do your research before buying. Also, when you're in the shop, make sure the bike they're selling you is put together correctly. Dealing with them will be a nightmare if not.

UPDATE: while Angel's response sounds nice, he wasn't helpful at all when I visited the store after this happened. Even when I pointed out the exact same flaw on other bikes they had yet to sell (which he literally fixed right in front of me), he did nothing to remedy the problem I had. Actions speak louder than words.< /review>< Pics>
